Reproducible Research: Peer Assessment 1 Ananya January 12, 2016 Loading and preprocessing the data The first step is to load the activity data set into a data frame df Overview of Data Head(df) and summary(df) provide the first few lines of the dataset and the summary statistics respectively. df <- read.csv("/Users/Ananya/Data-Science CE/Reproducible Research/Project/activity.csv", head=TRUE, na.strings="NA" ) head(df) ## steps date interval ## 1 NA 10/1/12 0 ## 2 NA 10/1/12 5 ## 3 NA 10/1/12 10 ## 4 NA 10/1/12 15 ## 5 NA 10/1/12 20 ## 6 NA 10/1/12 25 summary(df) ## steps date interval ## Min. : 0.00 10/1/12 : 288 Min. : 0.0 ## 1st Qu.: 0.00 10/10/12: 288 1st Qu.: 588.8 ## Median : 0.00 10/11/12: 288 Median :1177.5 ## Mean : 37.38 10/12/12: 288 Mean :1177.5 ## 3rd Qu.: 12.00 10/13/12: 288 3rd Qu.:1766.2 ## Max. :806.00 10/14/12: 288 Max. :2355.0 ## NA's :2304 (Other) :15840 Processing of Data remove the missing values, change the date column to reflect the date, subsetting the data set to new dataframe for further analysis df$date <-as.Date(df$date) df_missingremoved <-subset(df, !is.na(df$steps)) What is mean total number of steps taken per day? To solve this problem and to build histogram, we will first use tapply function which is used when a function is to be computed on a dataset (mean) and the results are to be displayed in appropriate form (Histogram in this case) dailyavg <- tapply(df_missingremoved$steps, df_missingremoved$date, sum, na.rm = TRUE) hist(x=dailyavg, col="green", breaks=20, xlab="Daily total steps", ylab="Frequency", main="The distribution of daily total (missing data ignored)") Mean of total number of steps taken per day mean(dailyavg) ## [1] 10729.94 Median of total number of steps taken per day median(dailyavg) ## [1] 10890 What is the average daily activity pattern? Make a time series plot (i.e. 𝚝𝚢𝚙𝚎 = “𝚕”) of the 5-minute interval (x-axis) and the average number of steps taken, averaged across all days (y-axis) avginterval <- tapply(df_missingremoved$steps, df_missingremoved$interval, mean, na.rm=TRUE, simplify=T) df_avgint <- data.frame(interval=as.integer(names(avginterval)), avg=avginterval) with(df_avgint, plot(interval, avg, type="l", xlab="5-minute intervals", ylab="average steps in the interval across all days")) The strategy does not need to be sophisticated. For example, you could use the mean/median for that day, or the mean for that 5-minute interval, etc. Using the mean for the 5 minute interval for filling missing values Create a new dataset that is equal to the original dataset but with the missing data filled in. df_impute <- df ndx <- is.na(df_impute$steps) int_avg <- tapply(df_missingremoved$steps, df_missingremoved$interval, mean, na.rm=TRUE, simplify=T) df_impute$steps[ndx] <- int_avg[as.character(df_impute$interval[ndx])] Make a histogram of the total number of steps taken each day and Calculate and report the mean and median total number of steps taken per day. Comparing with the previous mean and median from data where mising values where removed. Mean for imputed data is mean(new_dailysum) ## [1] 10739.01 Median for imputed data is median(new_dailysum) ## [1] 10766.19 So the mean for the imputed case is 10739.01 and the median is 10766.19. The missing removed values were 10729.94 and 10890. Since the mising values have been substituted by the mean value of the interval, the median is now more closer to the mean in the imputed case ## Are there differences in activity patterns between weekdays and weekends? ### Create a new factor variable in the dataset with two levels – “weekday” and “weekend” indicating whether a given date is a weekday or weekend day. weekday_end<- function(date) { day <- weekdays(date) if (day %in% c("Monday", "Tuesday", "Wednesday", "Thursday", "Friday")) return("weekday") else return("weekend") } weekday <- sapply(df_impute$date, weekday_end) df_impute$wk <- as.factor(weekday) head(df_impute) ## steps date interval wk ## 1 1.7169811 0010-01-12 0 weekday ## 2 0.3396226 0010-01-12 5 weekday ## 3 0.1320755 0010-01-12 10 weekday ## 4 0.1509434 0010-01-12 15 weekday ## 5 0.0754717 0010-01-12 20 weekday ## 6 2.0943396 0010-01-12 25 weekday Make a panel plot containing a time series plot (i.e. 𝚝𝚢𝚙𝚎 = “𝚕”) of the 5-minute interval (x-axis) and the average number of steps taken, averaged across all weekday days or weekend days (y-axis). wk_df <- aggregate(steps ~ wk+interval, data=df_impute, FUN=mean) library(lattice) xyplot(steps ~ interval
